Thule Society activist <a href="/wiki/Karl_Harrer" title="Karl Harrer">Karl Harrer</a> was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/German_Workers%27_Party" title="German Workers' Party">German Workers' Party</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gilbhard_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-gilbhard-98">[98]</a></sup> which later became the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>; some Nazi Party members like <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Hess" title="Rudolf Hess">Rudolf Hess</a> were listed as "guests" of the Thule Society, as was <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s mentor <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Eckart" title="Dietrich Eckart">Dietrich Eckart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> After their rise to power, the Nazis persecuted occultists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> While many Nazi Party leaders like Hitler and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a> were hostile to occultism, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> used <a href="/wiki/Karl_Maria_Wiligut" title="Karl Maria Wiligut">Karl Maria Wiligut</a> as a clairvoyant "and was regularly consulting for help in setting up the symbolic and ceremonial aspects of the SS" but not for important political decisions. By 1939, Wiligut was "forcibly retired from the SS" due to being institutionalised for insanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> On the other hand, the German hermetic magic order <a href="/wiki/Fraternitas_Saturni" title="Fraternitas Saturni">Fraternitas Saturni</a> was founded on Easter 1928 and it is one of the oldest continuously running magical groups in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_20th_century">Later 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Later 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Horned_God.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Horned_God.JPG/170px-Horned_God.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Horned_God.JPG/255px-Horned_God.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Horned_God.JPG/340px-Horned_God.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Horned_God.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sculpture of the <a href="/wiki/Horned_God" title="Horned God">Horned God</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wicca</a> found in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_Witchcraft" title="Museum of Witchcraft">Museum of Witchcraft</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boscastle" title="Boscastle">Boscastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1960s and 1970s, esotericism came to be increasingly associated with the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">growing counter-culture in the West</a>, whose adherents understood themselves in participating in a spiritual revolution that would mark the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Aquarius" title="Age of Aquarius">Age of Aquarius</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43-103">[103]</a></sup> By the 1980s, these currents of millenarian currents had come to be widely known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Age_movement" title="New Age movement">New Age movement</a>, and it became increasingly commercialised as business entrepreneurs exploited a growth in the spiritual market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43-103">[103]</a></sup> Conversely, other forms of esoteric thought retained the anti-commercial and counter-cultural sentiment of the 1960s and 1970s, namely the techno-shamanic movement promoted by figures such as <a href="/wiki/Terence_McKenna" title="Terence McKenna">Terence McKenna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Pinchbeck" title="Daniel Pinchbeck">Daniel Pinchbeck</a> which built on the work of anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Castaneda" title="Carlos Castaneda">Carlos Castaneda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a43-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>This trend was accompanied by the increased growth of <a href="/wiki/Modern_Paganism" title="Modern Paganism">modern Paganism</a>, a movement initially dominated by <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wicca</a>, the religion propagated by <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Gardner_(Wiccan)" title="Gerald Gardner (Wiccan)">Gerald Gardner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44-104">[104]</a></sup> Wicca was adopted by members of the second-wave feminist movement, most notably <a href="/wiki/Starhawk" title="Starhawk">Starhawk</a>, and developing into the <a href="/wiki/Goddess_movement" title="Goddess movement">Goddess movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44-104">[104]</a></sup> Wicca also greatly influenced the development of Pagan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-druidry" title="Neo-druidry">neo-druidry</a> and other forms of Celtic revivalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a44-104">[104]</a></sup> In response to Wicca there has also appeared literature and groups who label themselves followers of <a href="/wiki/Traditional_witchcraft" title="Traditional witchcraft">traditional witchcraft</a> in opposition to the growing visibility of Wicca and these claim older roots than the system proposed by <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Gardner_(Wiccan)" title="Gerald Gardner (Wiccan)">Gerald Gardner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Other trends which emerged in western occultism in the later 20th century were <a href="/wiki/Satanism" title="Satanism">satanism</a> as exposed by groups such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Satan" title="The Church of Satan">The Church of Satan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Set" title="Temple of Set">Temple of Set</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Chaos_magic" title="Chaos magic">chaos magick</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Illuminates_of_Thanateros" title="Illuminates of Thanateros">Illuminates of Thanateros</a> group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2013, Asprem and Granholm highlighted that "contemporary esotericism is intimately, and increasingly, connected with popular culture and new media."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20136_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20136-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Granholm noted that esoteric ideas and images could be found in many aspects of Western popular media, citing such examples as <i><a href="/wiki/Buffy_the_Vampire_Slayer" title="Buffy the Vampire Slayer">Buffy the Vampire Slayer</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hellblazer" title="Hellblazer">Hellblazer</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/His_Dark_Materials" title="His Dark Materials">His Dark Materials</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGranholm2013a31_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGranholm2013a31-109">[109]</a></sup> Granholm has argued that there are problems with the field in that it draws a distinction between esotericism and non-esoteric elements of culture which draw upon esotericism; citing the example of <a href="/wiki/Extreme_metal" title="Extreme metal">extreme metal</a>, he noted that it was incredibly difficult to differentiate between those artists who were "properly occult" and those who simply utilised occult themes and aesthetics in "a superficial way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGranholm2013b8.E2.80.939_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGranholm2013b8.E2.80.939-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writers interested in occult themes have adopted three different strategies for dealing with the subject: those who are knowledgeable on the subject including attractive images of the occult and occultists in their work, those who disguise occultism within "a web of intertextuality", and those who oppose it and seek to deconstruct it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBr.C3.AEnzeuSz.C3.B6nyi2011185_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBr.C3.AEnzeuSz.C3.B6nyi2011185-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_study">Academic study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Academic study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Academic_study_of_Western_esotericism" title="Academic study of Western esotericism">Academic study of Western esotericism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="752" data-file-width="1264" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg/290px-Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg/435px-Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg/580px-Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Warburg_Institute_from_Woburn_Square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
London's Warburg Institute was one of the first centres to encourage the academic study of Western esotericism</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The academic study of Western esotericism was pioneered in the early 20th century by historians of the ancient world and the European Renaissance, who came to recognise that – although it had been ignored by previous scholarship – the effect which pre-Christian and non-rational schools of thought had exerted on European society and culture was worthy of academic attention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20084_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20084-61">[61]</a></sup> One of the key centres for this was the <a href="/wiki/Warburg_Institute" title="Warburg Institute">Warburg Institute</a> in London, where scholars like <a href="/wiki/Frances_Yates" title="Frances Yates">Frances Yates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Wind" title="Edgar Wind">Edgar Wind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Cassirer" title="Ernst Cassirer">Ernst Cassirer</a>, and D. P. Walker began arguing that esoteric thought had had a greater effect on Renaissance culture than had been previously accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20084.E2.80.935_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20084.E2.80.935-112">[112]</a></sup> The work of Yates in particular, most notably her 1964 book <i><a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno_and_the_Hermetic_Tradition" title="Giordano Bruno and the Hermetic Tradition">Giordano Bruno and the Hermetic Tradition</a></i>, has been cited as "an important starting-point for modern scholarship on esotericism", succeeding "at one fell swoop in bringing scholarship onto a new track" by bringing wider awareness of the effect that esoteric ideas had on modern science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the instigation of the scholar <a href="/wiki/Henry_Corbin" title="Henry Corbin">Henry Corbin</a>, in 1965 the world's first academic post in the study of esotericism was established at the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_pratique_des_hautes_%C3%A9tudes" title="École pratique des hautes études">École pratique des hautes études</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sorbonne" title="Sorbonne">Sorbonne</a>, Paris; named the chair in the History of Christian Esotericism, its first holder was <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fran%C3%A7ois_Secret&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="François Secret (page does not exist)">François Secret</a>, a specialist in the Christian Kabbalah, although he had little interest in developing the wider study of esotericism as a field of research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ixVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201011_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ixVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201011-114">[114]</a></sup> In 1979 Faivre assumed Secret's chair at the Sorbonne, which was renamed the "History of Esoteric and Mystical Currents in Modern and Contemporary Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201012_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201012-115">[115]</a></sup> Faivre has since been cited as being responsible for developing the study of Western esotericism into a formalised field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVersluis20076Goodrick-Clarke20085_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVersluis20076Goodrick-Clarke20085-116">[116]</a></sup> with his 1992 work <i>L'ésotérisme</i> having been cited as marking "the beginning of the study of Western esotericism as an academic field of research".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013b179_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013b179-117">[117]</a></sup> He remained in the chair until 2002, when he was succeeded by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean-Pierre_Brach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean-Pierre Brach (page does not exist)">Jean-Pierre Brach</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faivre noted that there were two significant obstacles to establishing the field. One was that there was an engrained prejudice towards esotericism within academia, resulting in the widespread perception that the history of esotericism was not worthy of academic research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ix_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ix-118">[118]</a></sup> The second was that esotericism is a trans-disciplinary field, the study of which did not fit clearly within any particular discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ixVersluis20076_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ixVersluis20076-119">[119]</a></sup> As Hanegraaff noted, Western esotericism had to be studied as a separate field to religion, philosophy, science, and the arts, because while it "participates in all these fields" it does not squarely fit into any of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a1.E2.80.932_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013a1.E2.80.932-120">[120]</a></sup> Elsewhere, he noted that there was "probably no other domain in the humanities that has been so seriously neglected" as Western esotericism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013b198_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanegraaff2013b198-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1156" data-file-width="1116" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg/220px-Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg/330px-Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg/440px-Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wouter_Hanegraaff_2006_Alchemy_Conference.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prominent scholar of esotericism Wouter Hanegraaff</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1980, the U.S.-based <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hermetic_Academy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hermetic Academy (page does not exist)">Hermetic Academy</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._McDermott" title="Robert A. McDermott">Robert A. McDermott</a> as an outlet for American scholars interested in Western esotericism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xFaivreVoss199559_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xFaivreVoss199559-122">[122]</a></sup> From 1986 to 1990 members of the Hermetic Academy participated in panels at the annual meeting of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Religion" title="American Academy of Religion">American Academy of Religion</a> under the rubric of the "Esotericism and Perennialism Group".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xFaivreVoss199559_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994xFaivreVoss199559-122">[122]</a></sup> By 1994, Faivre could comment that the academic study of Western esotericism had taken off in France, Italy, England, and the United States, but he lamented the fact that it had not done so in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ix_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFaivre1994ix-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a> established a chair in the "History of Hermetic Philosophy and Related Currents", which was occupied by Hanegraaff,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201012.E2.80.9313_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3Von_Stuckrad2005b81Bergunder201012.E2.80.9313-123">[123]</a></sup> while in 2005 the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> created a chair in "Western Esotericism", which was taken by Goodrick-Clarke, who headed the Exeter Center for the Study of Esotericism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3Versluis20077_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005a3Versluis20077-124">[124]</a></sup> Thus, by 2008 there were three dedicated university chairs in the subject, with Amsterdam and Exeter also offering <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> programs in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20083_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodrick-Clarke20083-125">[125]</a></sup> Several conferences on the subject were held at the quintennial meetings of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Association_for_the_History_of_Religions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Association for the History of Religions (page does not exist)">International Association for the History of Religions</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005b81_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005b81-126">[126]</a></sup> while a peer-reviewed journal, <i><a href="/wiki/Aries_(journal)" title="Aries (journal)">Aries: Journal for the Study of Western Esotericism</a></i> began publication in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005b81_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Stuckrad2005b81-126">[126]</a></sup> 2001 also saw the foundation of the North American <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Association_for_the_Study_of_Esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Association for the Study of Esotericism (page does not exist)">Association for the Study of Esotericism</a> (ASE), with the <a href="/wiki/European_Society_for_the_Study_of_Western_Esotericism" title="European Society for the Study of Western Esotericism">European Society for the Study of Western Esotericism</a> (ESSWE) being established shortly after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVersluis20076_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVersluis20076-127">[127]</a></sup> Within a few years, Michael Bergunder expressed the view that it had become an established field within religious studies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergunder20109_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergunder20109-128">[128]</a></sup> with Asprem and Granholm observing that scholars within other sub-disciplines of religious studies had begun to take an interest in the work of scholars of esotericism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20131_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20131-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Asprem and Granholm noted that the study of esotericism had been dominated by historians and thus lacked the perspective of <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social scientists</a> examining contemporary forms of esotericism, a situation that they were attempting to correct through building links with scholars operating in <a href="/wiki/Pagan_studies" title="Pagan studies">Pagan studies</a> and the study of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_religious_movements" title="New religious movements">new religious movements</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20133.E2.80.934_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAspremGranholm20133.E2.80.934-130">[130]</a></sup> On the basis of the fact that "English culture and literature have been traditional strongholds of Western esotericism", in 2011 Pia Brînzeu and György Szönyi urged that <a href="/wiki/English_studies" title="English studies">English studies</a> also have a role in this interdisciplinary field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBr.C3.AEnzeuSz.C3.B6nyi2011184_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBr.C3.AEnzeuSz.C3.B6nyi2011184-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emic_and_etic_divisions">Emic and etic divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Emic and etic divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hanegraaff follows a distinction between an “emic” and an “etic” approach to religious studies. The emic approach is that of the alchemist or theosopher as an alchemist or theosopher. The etic approach is that of the scholar as an historian, a researcher, with a critical look. An empirical study of esotericism needs “emic material and etic interpretation”:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Emic denotes the believer’s point of view. On the part of the researcher, the reconstruction of this emic perspective requires an attitude of empathy which excludes personal biases as far as possible. Scholarly discourse about religion, on the other hand, is not emic but etic. Scholars may introduce their own terminology and make theoretical distinctions which are different from those of the believers themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Versluis" title="Arthur Versluis">Arthur Versluis</a> proposes approaching esotericism through a “sympathetic empiricism”:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Esotericism, given all its varied forms and its inherently multidimensional nature, cannot be conveyed without going beyond purely historical information: at minimum, the study of esotericism, and in particular mysticism, requires some degree of imaginative participation in what one is studying.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="459" data-file-width="378" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/EndlessKnot03d.png/23px-EndlessKnot03d.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/EndlessKnot03d.png/34px-EndlessKnot03d.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/EndlessKnot03d.png/46px-EndlessKnot03d.png 2x" width="23"/></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Spirituality" title="Portal:Spirituality">Spirituality portal</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_esotericism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
